   204Ôćĺ---
   205Ôćĺ
   206Ôćĺ## Lifecycle
   207Ôćĺ
   208Ôćĺ### Update Order
   209Ôćĺ
   210ÔćĺEach frame:
   211Ôćĺ
   212Ôćĺ1. **Collect all objects** ÔÇö Traverse tree, gather all non-dead objects
   213Ôćĺ2. **Early actions** (`/ U`) ÔÇö Run all early_action functions (tree order)
   214Ôćĺ3. **Main actions** (`/`) ÔÇö Run all action functions (tree order)
   215Ôćĺ4. **Late actions** (`/ L`) ÔÇö Run all late_action functions (tree order)
   216Ôćĺ5. **Cleanup** ÔÇö Remove dead objects, remove dead actions, call destroy() hooks
   217Ôćĺ
   218ÔćĺObjects created during the frame are collected in the next frame (they don't run actions in the frame they're created).
   219Ôćĺ
   220Ôćĺ### Action Phase Execution</code></pre>

</details>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   431Ôćĺ## Lua Syntax Features
   432Ôćĺ
   433Ôćĺ*These features were developed after analyzing [amulet.xyz](http://amulet.xyz), Ian MacLarty's Lua game engine. Amulet uses elegant operator overloading for scene graph construction. We adapted the patterns that fit Anchor's model while rejecting those that don't (like transforms-as-nodes and coroutine-based actions).*
   434Ôćĺ
   435Ôćĺ### Operator Overview
   436Ôćĺ
   437ÔćĺAnchor uses Lua's operator overloading to create a concise, pipeline-style syntax for object construction:
   438Ôćĺ
   439Ôćĺ| Operator | Operation | Description |
   440Ôćĺ|----------|-----------|-------------|
   441Ôćĺ| `^` | set/build | Assign properties (table) or run init code (function) |
   442Ôćĺ| `/` | action | Add action (runs every frame) |
   443Ôćĺ| `+` | add children | Add child objects to parent (parent-centric) |
   444Ôćĺ| `&gt;&gt;` | flow to parent | Add self to parent, **returns parent** (object-centric) |
   445Ôćĺ
   446ÔćĺThe `/` operator handles all action phases. Use the `U` and `L` helpers to mark early/late phases:
   447Ôćĺ
   448Ôćĺ| Pattern | Phase | When it runs |
   449Ôćĺ|---------|-------|--------------|
   450Ôćĺ| `/ U fn` | early | Before main actions |
   451Ôćĺ| `/ fn` | main | The main update phase |
   452Ôćĺ| `/ L fn` | late | After main actions (often drawing) |
   453Ôćĺ
   454ÔćĺOperators are ordered by precedence (highest to lowest: `^`, then `/`, then `+`, then `&gt;&gt;`), so they chain naturally left-to-right without parentheses.
   455Ôćĺ
   456Ôćĺ### Single-Letter Aliases
   457Ôćĺ
   458ÔćĺFor elegance, Anchor provides three single-letter aliases that look like runes:</code></pre>

</details>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   452Ôćĺ| `/ L fn` | late | After main actions (often drawing) |
   453Ôćĺ
   454ÔćĺOperators are ordered by precedence (highest to lowest: `^`, then `/`, then `+`, then `&gt;&gt;`), so they chain naturally left-to-right without parentheses.
   455Ôćĺ
   456Ôćĺ### Single-Letter Aliases
   457Ôćĺ
   458ÔćĺFor elegance, Anchor provides single-letter aliases that look like runes:
   459Ôćĺ
   460Ôćĺ| Alias | Purpose | Mnemonic |
   461Ôćĺ|-------|---------|----------|
   462Ôćĺ| `E` | Object constructor | Entity |
   463Ôćĺ| `U` | Early action helper | Under/underlying |
   464Ôćĺ| `L` | Late action helper | Late |
   465Ôćĺ| `X` | Named action helper | eXplicit |
   466Ôćĺ| `A` | Query descendants | All |
   467Ôćĺ
   468ÔćĺThese are defined in the engine:
   469Ôćĺ
   470Ôćĺ```lua
   471ÔćĺE = object
   472ÔćĺU = function(fn) return {__early = fn} end
   473ÔćĺL = function(fn) return {__late = fn} end
   474ÔćĺX = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end
   475Ôćĺ-- A is a method alias: self:A('tag') == self:all('tag')
   476Ôćĺ```
   477Ôćĺ
   478Ôćĺ**Future single-letter aliases** should prefer these characters, chosen for their angular, runic appearance (symmetrical, minimal roundness):
   479Ôćĺ
   480Ôćĺ```</code></pre>

   484Ôćĺ### Action Helpers: `U`, `L`, and `X`
   485Ôćĺ
   486ÔćĺThe `/` operator handles all action phases. Use helpers to specify phase or name:
   487Ôćĺ
   488Ôćĺ**Phase helpers (`U` and `L`):**
   489Ôćĺ```lua
   490Ôćĺself / U(function(self, dt) ... end)  -- early action
   491Ôćĺself / function(self, dt) ... end     -- main action (default)

   493Ôćĺ```
   494Ôćĺ
   495Ôćĺ**Named action helper (`X`):**

   497Ôćĺ-- Anonymous action (no name, can't be cancelled)

   499Ôćĺ

   503Ôćĺ-- Cancel later
   504Ôćĺself.seek:kill()
   505Ôćĺ```
   506Ôćĺ

   508Ôćĺ```lua

   543Ôćĺ
   544Ôćĺ### The `/` Operator: Actions
   545Ôćĺ
   546ÔćĺThe `/` operator adds actions. Use `U` and `L` helpers to specify early/late phases:
   547Ôćĺ
   548Ôćĺ```lua
   549Ôćĺobject() ^ {x = 100, y = 200}
   550Ôćĺ         / U(function(self, dt)
   551Ôćĺ               -- early: runs first
   552Ôćĺ           end)
   553Ôćĺ         / function(self, dt)
   554Ôćĺ               -- main update
   555Ôćĺ               game:circle(self.x, self.y, 10, color)
   556Ôćĺ           end
   557Ôćĺ         / L(function(self, dt)
   558Ôćĺ               -- late: runs last, good for drawing that needs final positions
   559Ôćĺ           end)
   560Ôćĺ```
   561Ôćĺ
   562ÔćĺActions return `true` to remove themselves (one-shot behavior). Returning `true` only removes the action, not the object.
   563Ôćĺ
   564Ôćĺ### The `&gt;&gt;` Operator: Flow to Parent
   565Ôćĺ
   566ÔćĺThe `&gt;&gt;` operator adds the left object as a child of the right object and **returns the parent**:</code></pre>

   653Ôćĺ```

   656Ôćĺ```lua

   658ÔćĺL = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- marks late phase
   659ÔćĺX = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end  -- marks name only
   660Ôćĺ```

   765Ôćĺ## YueScript Alternative
   766Ôćĺ
   767Ôćĺ*YueScript (evolved from MoonScript) is a language that compiles to Lua. It offers significant syntactic improvements: significant whitespace, `@` for self, `=&gt;` for methods with implicit self, no `end` keywords, `+=`/`-=` operators, and optional parentheses. The operator-based object construction style fits YueScript's aesthetic particularly well.*
   768Ôćĺ
   769Ôćĺ### Single-Letter Aliases in YueScript
   770Ôćĺ
   771ÔćĺThe same single-letter aliases work in YueScript:
   772Ôćĺ
   773Ôćĺ```yuescript
   774ÔćĺE = object                       -- Entity/object constructor
   775ÔćĺU = (fn) -&gt; {__early: fn}        -- early action helper (Under)
   776ÔćĺL = (fn) -&gt; {__late: fn}         -- late action helper (Late)
   777ÔćĺX = (name, fn) -&gt; {[name]: fn}   -- named action helper (eXplicit)
   778Ôćĺ-- A is a method alias: @\A 'tag' == @\all 'tag'
   779Ôćĺ```
   780Ôćĺ
   781Ôćĺ### Syntax Comparison
   782Ôćĺ
   783Ôćĺ| Lua | YueScript |</code></pre>

</details>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   953Ôćĺ## YueScript Class System Integration
   954Ôćĺ
   955ÔćĺAnchor uses YueScript's native class system with inheritance. This section details how the operator-based syntax integrates with YueScript classes.
   956Ôćĺ
   957Ôćĺ### Base Object Class
   958Ôćĺ
   959ÔćĺThe `object` class is the root of all game objects. It provides the core functionality and operators:
   960Ôćĺ
   961Ôćĺ```yuescript
   962Ôćĺclass object
   963Ôćĺ  -- Class-level callback: propagate metamethods to child classes
   964Ôćĺ  @__inherited: (child) =&gt;
   965Ôćĺ    -- Copy operator metamethods to child's base
   966Ôćĺ    for mm in *{'__pow', '__div', '__add', '__shr'}
   967Ôćĺ      unless rawget child.__base, mm
   968Ôćĺ        child.__base[mm] = @__base[mm]
   969Ôćĺ    -- Also propagate __inherited itself
   970Ôćĺ    unless rawget child, '__inherited'
   971Ôćĺ      child.__inherited = @@__inherited
   972Ôćĺ
   973Ôćĺ  -- Constructor
   974Ôćĺ  new: (name, args) =&gt;
   975Ôćĺ    @name = name
   976Ôćĺ    @children = {}
   977Ôćĺ    @tags = {}
   978Ôćĺ    @dead = false
   979Ôćĺ    if args
   980Ôćĺ      for k, v in pairs args
   981Ôćĺ        @[k] = v
... [148 more lines]</code></pre>

</details>

<details>
<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/docs/ANCHOR.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
  1213Ôćĺ  late_update: (dt) =&gt;
  1214Ôćĺ    game\circle @x, @y, @radius, @color
  1215Ôćĺ```
  1216Ôćĺ
  1217Ôćĺ**Methods and actions both run.** If an object has both an `update:` method and `/` actions, the method runs first, then the actions. This allows class-defined behavior to coexist with dynamically added behavior.
  1218Ôćĺ
  1219ÔćĺNote: The `%` and `//` operators are no longer used. All actions use `/` with `U` and `L` helpers for phase selection.
  1220Ôćĺ
  1221Ôćĺ### Colliders, Springs, and Timers Are Tree Objects
  1222Ôćĺ
  1223ÔćĺColliders, springs, and timers are all proper tree objects (classes extending `object`). They live in `@children` like any other child, and die when their parent dies.</code></pre>

   177Ôćĺ-- A is a method alias: self:A('tag') == self:all('tag')

   497Ôćĺ**Multiple `^` operators:** When chaining multiple `^`, group all initialization before action operators:
   498Ôćĺ```lua
   499Ôćĺ-- Good: all init together, then actions
   500ÔćĺE() ^ {x = 100, y = 200}
   501Ôćĺ   ^ function(self) self + timer() end
   502Ôćĺ   / function(self, dt) ... end
   503Ôćĺ   &gt;&gt; arena
   504Ôćĺ
   505Ôćĺ-- Bad: init split across the chain
   506ÔćĺE() ^ {x = 100}
   507Ôćĺ   / function(self, dt) ... end
   508Ôćĺ   ^ function(self) self + timer() end -- init after action, harder to follow
   509Ôćĺ   &gt;&gt; arena
   510Ôćĺ```
   511Ôćĺ
   512Ôćĺ### Named vs Anonymous
   513Ôćĺ
   514ÔćĺThe tree automatically manages named children: adding a child with a name that already exists kills the old child first. This provides cancellation and replacement without explicit tag systems.</code></pre>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   821Ôćĺ#### No Bureaucracy
   822Ôćĺ
   823ÔćĺImports, exports, dependency injection, configuration objects, registration systems ÔÇö these are bureaucracy. They may be necessary in large teams, but for solo development they're friction.
   824Ôćĺ
   825ÔćĺAnchor prefers:
   826Ôćĺ- Globals that are just available (`an`, `E`, `U`, `L`, `X`, `A`)
   827Ôćĺ- Direct mutation over message passing
   828Ôćĺ- Explicit calls over implicit event systems
   829Ôćĺ- Things that work without setup
   830Ôćĺ
   831Ôćĺ**When evaluating features:** Does this require ceremony to use, or does it just work?
   832Ôćĺ
   833Ôćĺ#### Alien But Right</code></pre>

</details>

<details>
<summary><code>Edit (/home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md)</code></summary>

<pre><code>The file /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/.claude/CLAUDE.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:
   829Ôćĺ- Things that work without setup
   830Ôćĺ
   831Ôćĺ**When evaluating features:** Does this require ceremony to use, or does it just work?
   832Ôćĺ
   833Ôćĺ#### Alien But Right
   834Ôćĺ
   835ÔćĺThe operator syntax (`^`, `/`, `+`, `&gt;&gt;`) and single-letter aliases (`E`, `U`, `L`, `X`, `A`) are deliberately unusual. Inspired by Hoon's rune system ÔÇö symbols that seem foreign at first but become natural with use.
   836Ôćĺ
   837ÔćĺThe goal isn't familiarity, it's terseness and visual distinctiveness. `E 'player'` is weirder than `Object.new('player')` but it's shorter and once learned, instantly recognizable.
   838Ôćĺ
   839ÔćĺSingle-letter aliases follow a preference for angular, symmetrical letters: E, X, A, T, L, V, U, Y, I, H. Avoid round letters (O, Q, C, G).
   840Ôćĺ
   841Ôćĺ**When evaluating features:** Does this earn its complexity? Is the weirdness worth it?
   842Ôćĺ
   843Ôćĺ### Language Boundary Philosophy</code></pre>

<pre><code>1Ôćĺ# Anchor Implementation Plan
     2Ôćĺ
     3ÔćĺC engine with YueScript scripting, OpenGL rendering, targeting Windows, Linux, and Web.
     4Ôćĺ
     5Ôćĺ---
     6Ôćĺ
     7Ôćĺ## Summary of Key Decisions
     8Ôćĺ
     9Ôćĺ| Area | Decision | Rationale |
    10Ôćĺ|------|----------|-----------|
    11Ôćĺ| Renderer | OpenGL | Smooth rotation, additive blending, performance headroom, console-portable |
    12Ôćĺ| Audio | TBD (miniaudio or SoLoud) | Need pitch shifting; SDL_mixer insufficient |
    13Ôćĺ| Physics | Box2D 3.1 | Already used, true ball-to-ball collisions needed |
    14Ôćĺ| Scripting | Lua 5.4 + YueScript | Build-time compilation with `-r` flag for line numbers |
    15Ôćĺ| Timestep | Fixed 60fps | Determinism matters for potential replay support |
    16Ôćĺ| Resolution | Per-game configurable | 480├Ś270, 640├Ś360, or custom; integer scaling |
    17Ôćĺ| C Structure | Single anchor.c | Monolithic file, easier navigation |
    18Ôćĺ| Resources | Live forever | Games are small enough; no unloading needed |
    19Ôćĺ| Distribution | Single executable | Assets embedded |
    20Ôćĺ
    21Ôćĺ---
    22Ôćĺ
    23Ôćĺ## Build Strategy

    30Ôćĺgame.yue ÔöÇÔöÇÔľ║ yue -r ÔöÇÔöÇÔľ║ game.lua ÔöÇÔöÇÔľ║ embedded in executable

<pre><code>470Ôćĺ
   471Ôćĺ### 10.1 YueScript Build Integration
   472Ôćĺ- [ ] Install YueScript compiler
   473Ôćĺ- [ ] Add compilation step to build.bat/build.sh
   474Ôćĺ- [ ] Use `-r` flag for line number preservation
   475Ôćĺ- [ ] Verify errors report correct .yue line numbers
   476Ôćĺ
   477Ôćĺ### 10.2 Base Object Class
   478ÔćĺImplement in `yue/object.yue`:
   479Ôćĺ- Constructor with name/args
   480Ôćĺ- Tree operations: `add_child`, `remove_child`, `kill`
   481Ôćĺ- Tagging: `tag`, `is`, `all` / `A`
   482Ôćĺ- Links: `link` for horizontal dependencies
   483Ôćĺ- Operators: `^`, `%`, `/`, `//`, `+`, `&gt;&gt;`
   484Ôćĺ- `__inherited` hook to propagate operators to child classes
   485Ôćĺ
   486Ôćĺ**Ask developer before implementing details.**
   487Ôćĺ
   488Ôćĺ### Engine Object Pattern
   489Ôćĺ
   490ÔćĺTimer, spring, and collider are examples of **engine objects** ÔÇö classes that wrap C-side resources. All engine objects follow this pattern:
   491Ôćĺ
   492Ôćĺ1. They extend the base `object` class
   493Ôćĺ2. They're instantiated and added as children: `@ + timer()`
   494Ôćĺ3. They're named after themselves by default (e.g., `timer()` has `name = 'timer'`)
   495Ôćĺ4. Parent accesses them via that name: `@timer:after(...)`
   496Ôćĺ5. They implement `destroy()` to clean up C-side resources when killed
   497Ôćĺ
   498ÔćĺThis pattern applies to any future engine objects (particles, audio sources, etc.).
   499Ôćĺ
... [111 more lines]</code></pre>

</details>

> `Bash (mv /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/yue/operator_comparison.yue /home/adn/a327ex/Anchor/y...)`

Done. All three documents have been updated to reflect the new operator system:

**Summary of changes:**

| Old | New |
|-----|-----|
| `%` operator for early actions | `/ U(fn)` or `/ U('name', fn)` |
| `//` operator for late actions | `/ L(fn)` or `/ L('name', fn)` |
| `__mod` and `__idiv` metamethods | Single `__div` that detects U/L/X helpers |

**New alias set:**
- **E** = object (Entity)
- **U** = early action helper (Under/underlying)
- **L** = late action helper (Late)
- **X** = named action helper (eXplicit)
- **A** = all() query method alias (All)

**Files updated:**
- `docs/ANCHOR.md` ÔÇö operator tables, examples, reference implementation
- `docs/ANCHOR_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md` ÔÇö Phase 10 specifications
- `.claude/CLAUDE.md` ÔÇö code patterns, aliases, context brief
- `yue/examples.yue` ÔÇö renamed from operator_comparison.yue, cleaned up header

> Please remove all mentions of % and //, in one section you mention that they're no longer used, but anyone reading the documents doesn't need that information about the past.

> I think that was the only problem that you mentioned that I thought we had to fix. Great, anything else you have to say about the engine that you feel is wrong?

~~~
Looking back through everything, I think the design is solid now. The main issues we addressed were:

1. **`add_child` Ôćĺ `add`** ÔÇö Fixed the method name inconsistency
2. **`%` and `//` Ôćĺ `/ U` and `/ L`** ÔÇö Unified all actions under `/` with helpers

One minor thing I noticed but didn't flag: the "Single-Letter Aliases" section shows simplified definitions:

```lua
U = function(fn) return {__early = fn} end
L = function(fn) return {__late = fn} end
```

But the actual usage supports two forms: `U(fn)` and `U('name', fn)`. The full implementation in the reference section handles both, but the overview only shows the single-argument form.

This is probably fine ÔÇö the overview is meant to be simple, and the "Action Helpers" section explains the full usage. But if you want complete accuracy in the overview, the signatures would be:

```lua
U = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- supports U(fn) or U('name', fn)
L = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end  -- supports L(fn) or L('name', fn)
```

Other than that, I don't see any remaining issues. The philosophy is coherent, the tree model is elegant, the operator syntax is consistent, and the documentation matches the reference implementation.
~~~

   168Ôćĺ### Single-Letter Aliases
   169Ôćĺ
   170ÔćĺAnchor provides single-letter aliases that look like runes:
   171Ôćĺ
   172Ôćĺ```lua
   173ÔćĺE = object                                        -- Entity/object
   174ÔćĺU = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end              -- U(fn) or U('name', fn)
   175ÔćĺL = function(name_or_fn, fn) ... end              -- L(fn) or L('name', fn)
   176ÔćĺX = function(name, fn) return {[name] = fn} end   -- eXplicit/named
   177Ôćĺ-- A is a method alias: self:A('tag') == self:all('tag')
   178Ôćĺ```
   179Ôćĺ
   180ÔćĺIn YueScript:
   181Ôćĺ```yuescript
   182ÔćĺE = object
   183ÔćĺU = (name_or_fn, fn) -&gt; ...  -- U(fn) or U('name', fn)
   184ÔćĺL = (name_or_fn, fn) -&gt; ...  -- L(fn) or L('name', fn)
   185ÔćĺX = (name, fn) -&gt; {[name]: fn}
   186Ôćĺ```
   187Ôćĺ
   188Ôćĺ**Future single-letter aliases** should prefer these characters, chosen for their angular, runic appearance (symmetrical, minimal roundness):
   189Ôćĺ
   190Ôćĺ```</code></pre>

   767Ôćĺ*YueScript (evolved from MoonScript) is a language that compiles to Lua. It offers significant syntactic improvements: significant whitespace, `@` for self, `=&gt;` for methods with implicit self, no `end` keywords, `+=`/`-=` operators, and optional parentheses. The operator-based object construction style fits YueScript's aesthetic particularly well.*
   768Ôćĺ
   769Ôćĺ### Single-Letter Aliases in YueScript
   770Ôćĺ
   771ÔćĺThe same single-letter aliases work in YueScript:
   772Ôćĺ
   773Ôćĺ```yuescript
   774ÔćĺE = object                        -- Entity/object constructor
   775ÔćĺU = (name_or_fn, fn) -&gt; ...       -- U(fn) or U('name', fn)
   776ÔćĺL = (name_or_fn, fn) -&gt; ...       -- L(fn) or L('name', fn)
   777ÔćĺX = (name, fn) -&gt; {[name]: fn}    -- named action helper (eXplicit)
   778Ôćĺ-- A is a method alias: @\A 'tag' == @\all 'tag'
   779Ôćĺ```
   780Ôćĺ
   781Ôćĺ### Syntax Comparison
   782Ôćĺ
   783Ôćĺ| Lua | YueScript |</code></pre>
